     <p>The <b>University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign</b> (<b>U of I</b>, <b>University of Illinois</b>, <b>UIUC</b>, or simply <b>Illinois</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> research-intensive university in the U.S. state of <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>. A land-grant university, it is the flagship campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_system" title="University of Illinois system">University of Illinois system</a>. The University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign is the second oldest public university in the state (after <a href="/wiki/Illinois_State_University" title="Illinois State University">Illinois State University</a>), and is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>. It is considered a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>. The university is designated as a RU/VH Research University (very high research activities).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus library system possesses the second-largest university library in the United States and the fifth-largest in the country overall.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university comprises 17 colleges that offer more than 150 programs of study. Additionally, the university operates an extension<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> that serves 2.7 million registrants per year around the state of Illinois and beyond. The campus holds 286 buildings on 1,468 acres (594&nbsp;ha) in the <a href="/wiki/Twin_cities_(geographical_proximity)" title="Twin cities (geographical proximity)">twin cities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Champaign,_Illinois" title="Champaign, Illinois">Champaign</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urbana,_Illinois" title="Urbana, Illinois">Urbana</a>; its annual operating budget in 2011 was over $1.7 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Illinois_Presidents" title="List of University of Illinois Presidents">List of University of Illinois Presidents</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Act" title="Morrill Act" class="mw-redirect">Morrill Act</a> of 1862 granted each state in the United States a portion of land on which to establish a major public state university, one which could teach agriculture, mechanic arts, and military training, &quot;without excluding other scientific and classical studies.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Illini_years_pg6_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illini_years_pg6-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> This phrase would engender controversy over the University's initial academic philosophies, polarizing the relationship between the people of Illinois and the University's first president, <a href="/wiki/John_Milton_Gregory" title="John Milton Gregory">John Milton Gregory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Champaign-Urbana_area_IMG_0992.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Champaign-Urbana_area_IMG_0992.jpg/220px-Champaign-Urbana_area_IMG_0992.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Champaign-Urbana_area_IMG_0992.jpg/330px-Champaign-Urbana_area_IMG_0992.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Champaign-Urbana_area_IMG_0992.jpg/440px-Champaign-Urbana_area_IMG_0992.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Champaign-Urbana_area_IMG_0992.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Hallene Gateway. The inscription reads, &quot;Learning &amp; Labor,&quot; the University motto.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:John_Milton_Gregory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/John_Milton_Gregory.jpg/170px-John_Milton_Gregory.jpg" width="170" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/John_Milton_Gregory.jpg/255px-John_Milton_Gregory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/John_Milton_Gregory.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:John_Milton_Gregory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> John Milton Gregory
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>After a fierce bidding war between a number of Illinois cities, <a href="/wiki/Urbana,_Illinois" title="Urbana, Illinois">Urbana</a> was selected in 1867 as the site for the new school.<sup id="cite_ref-Illini_years_pg6_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illini_years_pg6-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> From the beginning, Gregory's desire to establish an institution firmly grounded in the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts" class="mw-redirect">liberal arts</a> tradition was at odds with many State residents and lawmakers who wanted the university to offer classes based solely around &quot;industrial education&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-manifesto_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manifesto-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The University finally opened for classes on March 2, 1868, with only two faculty members and a small group of students. The debate between the liberal arts curriculum and industrial education continued in the University's inaugural address, as Dr. Newton Bateman outlined the various interpretations of the Morrill Act in his speech.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Gregory's thirteen-year tenure would be marred by this debate. Clashes between Gregory and legislators and lawmakers forced his resignation from his post as president in 1880, saying &quot;[I am] staggering under too heavy a load of cares, and irritated by what has sometimes seemed as needless opposition.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Today, Gregory is largely credited with establishing the University and forming it into the major interdisciplinary university it is today. Gregory's grave is still located on the Urbana campus, situated between <a href="/wiki/UIUC_Main_Campus#Altgeld_Hall" title="UIUC Main Campus" class="mw-redirect">Altgeld Hall</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_Main_Campus#Henry_Administration_Building" title="UIUC Main Campus" class="mw-redirect">Henry Administration Building</a>. His marker (mimicking the epitaph of British architect <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">Christopher Wren</a>) reads, &quot;If you seek his monument, look about you.&quot;</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:World_War_One_Personnel_Squadron_32_Champaign_Illinois.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a5/World_War_One_Personnel_Squadron_32_Champaign_Illinois.jpg/220px-World_War_One_Personnel_Squadron_32_Champaign_Illinois.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a5/World_War_One_Personnel_Squadron_32_Champaign_Illinois.jpg/330px-World_War_One_Personnel_Squadron_32_Champaign_Illinois.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a5/World_War_One_Personnel_Squadron_32_Champaign_Illinois.jpg/440px-World_War_One_Personnel_Squadron_32_Champaign_Illinois.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:World_War_One_Personnel_Squadron_32_Champaign_Illinois.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The School of Military Aeronautics on campus on January 30, 1918
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Following World War II, under president David Henry, the university experienced rapid growth?doubling its enrollment and significantly improving its academic standing.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> This period was also marked by large growth in the Graduate College and increased federal support of scientific and technological research. The state of Illinois supplied roughly two-thirds of the university's budget while the federal government funded 90% of research.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> In recent years, state support has declined from 4.5% of the state's tax appropriations in 1980 to 2.28% in 2011, a nearly 50% decline.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, the university's budget has strongly shifted away from relying on state support with nearly 84% of the budget now coming from other sources.<sup id="cite_ref-illinois1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illinois1-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution_of_name">Evolution of name</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Evolution of name">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The original name in 1867 was &quot;Illinois Industrial University.&quot; In 1885, the Illinois Industrial University officially changed its name to the University of Illinois, reflecting its holistic agricultural, mechanical, and liberal arts curricula.<sup id="cite_ref-manifesto_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manifesto-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> This remained the official name for nearly 100 years, until it was changed to The University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign in 1982, ostensibly to establish a separate identity for the campus within the University of Illinois system. However, after a century's use, UIUC continues to be known and referred to as &quot;The University of Illinois&quot;, or just &quot;Illinois&quot;; this is true in both the media,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> and on many of UIUC's web pages.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Starting in 2008, the university began strongly rebranding itself as &quot;Illinois&quot; rather than UIUC, changing the website URL from uiuc.edu to Illinois.edu as well as all email addresses.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_schools">Colleges and schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colleges and schools">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>University of Illinois offers study through 17 colleges. Advanced undergraduate students may participate in a rigorous course of study through the <i>James Scholar Honors Program</i> and earn highest distinctions with <a href="/wiki/University_Honors_(University_of_Illinois)" title="University Honors (University of Illinois)" class="mw-redirect">University Honors</a>.</p> 
     <div class="references" style="-moz-column-count:3; column-count:3"> 
      <ul> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Agriculture,_Consumer,_and_Environmental_Sciences" title="UIUC College of Agriculture, Consumer, and Environmental Sciences">College of Agriculture, Consumer, and Environmental Sciences</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Applied_Health_Sciences" title="UIUC College of Applied Health Sciences">College of Applied Health Sciences</a></li>

     </div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_the_University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign" title="Campus of the University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign">Campus of the University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The campus is known for its landscape and architecture, as well as distinctive landmarks.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> It was identified as one of 50 college or university 'works of art' by T.A. Gaines in his book <i>The Campus as a Work of Art</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Foellinger_Auditorium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Foellinger_Auditorium.jpg/200px-Foellinger_Auditorium.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Foellinger_Auditorium.jpg/300px-Foellinger_Auditorium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Foellinger_Auditorium.jpg/400px-Foellinger_Auditorium.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Foellinger_Auditorium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Foellinger Auditorium
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The main research and academic facilities are divided almost exactly between the twin cities of <a href="/wiki/Urbana,_Illinois" title="Urbana, Illinois">Urbana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Champaign,_Illinois" title="Champaign, Illinois">Champaign</a>. The <a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Agriculture,_Consumer,_and_Environmental_Sciences" title="UIUC College of Agriculture, Consumer, and Environmental Sciences">College of Agriculture, Consumer, and Environmental Sciences'</a> research fields stretch south from Urbana and Champaign into <a href="/wiki/Savoy,_Illinois" title="Savoy, Illinois">Savoy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Champaign_County,_Illinois" title="Champaign County, Illinois">Champaign County</a>. The university maintains formal gardens and a conference center in nearby <a href="/wiki/Monticello,_Illinois" title="Monticello, Illinois">Monticello</a> at <a href="/wiki/Robert_Allerton_Park" title="Robert Allerton Park">Allerton Park</a>.</p> 
     <p>U of I is one of the few educational institutions to own an airport.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_Willard_Airport" title="University of Illinois Willard Airport">Willard Airport</a>, named for former University of Illinois president Arthur Cutts Willard, is located in Savoy. It was completed in 1945 and began service in 1954. Willard Airport is home to University research projects and the University's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_Institute_of_Aviation" title="University of Illinois Institute of Aviation">Institute of Aviation</a>, along with flights from American Airlines.</p> 
     <p>The campus is based on the <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quadrangle</a> design popular at many universities. Four main quads compose the center of the university and are arranged from north to south. The Beckman Quadrangle and the <a href="/wiki/John_Bardeen" title="John Bardeen">John Bardeen</a> Quadrangle occupy the center of the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_Engineering_Campus" title="UIUC Engineering Campus">Engineering Campus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Boneyard_Creek" title="Boneyard Creek">Boneyard Creek</a> flows through the John Bardeen Quadrangle, paralleling <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Street_(UIUC)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Green Street (UIUC) (page does not exist)">Green Street</a>. The Beckman Quadrangle is primarily composed of research units and laboratories, and features a large solar calendar consisting of an obelisk and several copper fountains. The Main Quadrangle and South Quadrangle follow immediately after the John Bardeen Quad. The former makes up a large part of the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Liberal_Arts_and_Sciences" title="UIUC College of Liberal Arts and Sciences">Liberal Arts and Sciences</a> portion of the campus, while the latter comprises many of the buildings of the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Agriculture,_Consumer,_and_Environmental_Sciences" title="UIUC College of Agriculture, Consumer, and Environmental Sciences">College of ACES</a> spread across the campus map.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In October 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Endowments_Institute" title="Sustainable Endowments Institute" class="mw-redirect">Sustainable Endowments Institute</a> gave the campus a grade of B for sustainability in its 2011 College Sustainability Report Card. Strengths noted in the report included the campus's adoption of <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> gold standards for all new construction and major renovations and its public accessibility to endowment investment information. The university makes a list of endowment holdings and its shareholder voting record available to the public. The weaknesses are areas such as student involvement and investment priorities. The student sustainability committee is empowered to allocate funding from a clean energy technology fee and a sustainable campus environment fee, while the university aims to optimize investment return but has not made any public statements about investigating or investing in renewable energy funds or community development loan funds. However, the biggest weakness of the university's sustainability is its shareholder engagement, as the university has not made any public statements about active ownership or a proxy voting policy.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In his remarks on the creation of the Office of Sustainability in September 2008, Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Richard_Herman" title="Richard Herman">Richard Herman</a> stated, &quot;I want this institution to be the leader in sustainability.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2008, he signed the American College and University Presidents Climate Commitment, committing the University of Illinois to take steps &quot;in pursuit of climate neutrality.&quot;<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign is often regarded as a world-leading magnet for engineering and sciences (both applied and basic).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Having been classified into the category comprehensive doctoral with medical/veterinary and very high research activity,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/The_Carnegie_Foundation_for_the_Advancement_of_Teaching" title="The Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching" class="mw-redirect">The Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching</a>, Illinois offers a wide range of disciplines in undergraduate and postgraduate programs. It is also listed as one of the Top 25 American Research Universities by <a href="/wiki/The_Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="The Center for Measuring University Performance" class="mw-redirect">The Center for Measuring University Performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Beside annual influx of grants and sponsored projects, the university manages an extensive modern research infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has been a leader in computer based education and hosted the <a href="/wiki/PLATO_(computer_system)" title="PLATO (computer system)">PLATO</a> project, which was a precursor to the internet and resulted in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Plasma_display" title="Plasma display">plasma display</a>.</p> 
     <p>The university hosts the <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Supercomputing_Applications" title="National Center for Supercomputing Applications">National Center for Supercomputing Applications</a> (NCSA), which created <a href="/wiki/Mosaic_(web_browser)" title="Mosaic (web browser)">Mosaic</a>, the first graphical <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">Web</a> browser, the foundation upon which Mozilla Firefox and Microsoft Internet Explorer are based, the <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_server" title="Apache HTTP server" class="mw-redirect">Apache HTTP server</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NCSA_Telnet" title="NCSA Telnet">NCSA Telnet</a>. The Parallel@Illinois program hosts several programs in <a href="/wiki/Parallel_computing" title="Parallel computing">parallel computing</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/UPCRC_Illinois" title="UPCRC Illinois">Universal Parallel Computing Research Center</a>. The university contracted with <a href="/wiki/Cray" title="Cray">Cray</a> to build the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>-funded supercomputer <a href="/wiki/Blue_Waters" title="Blue Waters">Blue Waters</a> after <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> backed out in August 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Blue_Waters" title="Blue Waters">Blue Waters</a> will be capable of sustained performance of one quadrillion calculations per second and peak performance of more than eleven quadrillion calculations per second.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The system also boasts the largest online storage system in the world with more than 25 petabytes of usable space.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The university whimsically celebrated January 12, 1997 as the &quot;birthday&quot; of <a href="/wiki/HAL_9000" title="HAL 9000">HAL 9000</a>, the fictional supercomputer from the novel and film <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey" title="2001: A Space Odyssey">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i>; in both works, HAL credits &quot;Urbana, Illinois&quot; as his place of operational origin.</p> 
     <p>In 1952, the university built the <a href="/wiki/ILLIAC" title="ILLIAC">ILLIAC</a> (Illinois Automatic Computer), the first computer built and owned entirely by an educational institution. U of I is also the site of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">Department of Energy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Center_for_the_Simulation_of_Advanced_Rockets" title="Center for the Simulation of Advanced Rockets">Center for the Simulation of Advanced Rockets</a>, an institute which has employed graduate and faculty researchers in the physical sciences and mathematics. It performs <a href="/wiki/Materials_science" title="Materials science">materials science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Condensed_matter_physics" title="Condensed matter physics">condensed matter physics</a> research, and is home to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Frederick_Seitz_Materials_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Frederick Seitz Materials Research Laboratory (page does not exist)">Frederick Seitz Materials Research Laboratory</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Micro_and_Nanotechnology_Laboratory" title="Micro and Nanotechnology Laboratory" class="mw-redirect">Micro and Nanotechnology Laboratory</a>. Two complexes for research and teaching recently opened, <a href="/wiki/Siebel_Center_for_Computer_Science" title="Siebel Center for Computer Science" class="mw-redirect">Siebel Center for Computer Science</a> in 2004 and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Institute_for_Genomic_Biology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Institute for Genomic Biology (page does not exist)">Institute for Genomic Biology</a> in 2006. <a href="/wiki/Beckman_Institute" title="Beckman Institute">The Beckman Institute for Advanced Science and Technology</a>, however, is still the largest interdisciplinary facility on campus with 313,000 square feet (29,100&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>). The university also conducts agricultural and horticultural research.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Prairie_Research_Institute" title="Prairie Research Institute">Prairie Research Institute</a> is located on campus and is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Natural_History_Survey" title="Illinois Natural History Survey">Illinois Natural History Survey</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Illinois_State_Geological_Survey&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Illinois State Geological Survey (page does not exist)">Illinois State Geological Survey</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.isws.illinois.edu">Illinois State Water Survey</a>, and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.istc.illinois.edu">Illinois Sustainable Technology Center</a> which have been located on the campus throughout their histories, but were Illinois state government agencies until the formation of the Institute within the University in 2008. Since 1957 the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.isas.illinois.edu">Illinois Transportation Archaeological Research Program (ITARP)</a> has conducted archaeological and historical compliance work for the Illinois Department of Transportation. In 2010, ITARP became the Illinois State Archaeological Survey (ISAS) and joined the <a href="/wiki/Prairie_Research_Institute" title="Prairie Research Institute">Prairie Research Institute</a>. Researchers at the Prairie Research Institute are engaged in basic and applied research in agriculture and forestry, biodiversity and ecosystem health, atmospheric resources, climate and associated natural hazards, cultural resources and history of human settlements, disease and public health, emerging pests, fisheries and wildlife, energy and industrial technology, mineral resources, pollution prevention and mitigation, and water resources. The Institute is a repository of specimens which serve as research collections on the Illinois environment. The <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Natural_History_Survey" title="Illinois Natural History Survey">Illinois Natural History Survey</a> biological collections include insects, crustaceans, molluscs, annelids, reptiles and amphibians, birds, mammals, algae, bryophytes, fungi, and vascular plants; the insect collection is among the largest in North America and digitization collections is currently underway with funding from the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>. The Illinois State Geological Survey houses the legislatively mandated <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.isgs.illinois.edu/sections/indust-min/samplib/samplib-home.shtml">Illinois Geological Samples Library</a>, a repository for drill-hole samples in Illinois, including cores drilled for mineral exploration and geologic investigations, as well as paleontological collections. ISAS serves as a repository for a large collection of Illinois archaeological artifacts now numbering over 17,000 boxes. One of the major collections is from the Cahokia Mounds,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> for which ISAS has over 550 boxes. An on-line database will soon be mounted for the Cahokia collection, funded by a 2008?2010 National Endowment for the Humanities grant.</p> 
     <p>In the February 24, 2004 talk as part of his Five Campus Tour (Harvard, MIT, Cornell, Carnegie-Mellon and Illinois),<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> titled &quot;Software Breakthroughs: Solving the Toughest Problems in Computer Science,&quot; <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a> has mentioned that Microsoft hires more graduates from the University of Illinois than from any other university in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Alumnus <a href="/w/index.php?title=William_M._Holt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="William M. Holt (page does not exist)">William M. Holt</a>, a Senior Vice-President of <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>, also mentioned in a campus talk in September 27, 2007 entitled &quot;R&amp;D to Deliver Practical Results: Extending Moore's Law&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> that Intel hires more PhD graduates from the University of Illinois than from any other university in the country.</p> 
     <p>In 2007, the university-hosted research <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Condensed_Matter_Theory" title="Institute for Condensed Matter Theory">Institute for Condensed Matter Theory</a> (ICMT) was launched, with the director <a href="/wiki/Paul_Goldbart" title="Paul Goldbart">Paul Goldbart</a> and the chief scientist <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Leggett" title="Anthony Leggett" class="mw-redirect">Anthony Leggett</a>. ICMT is currently located at the Engineering Science Building on campus.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Ten_Committee_on_Institutional_Cooperation">Big Ten Committee on Institutional Cooperation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Big Ten Committee on Institutional Cooperation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>University of Illinois is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Institutional_Cooperation" title="Committee on Institutional Cooperation">Committee on Institutional Cooperation</a>. The Committee on Institutional Cooperation (CIC) is the academic consortium of the universities in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> plus former conference member, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>. The initiative also allows students at participating institutions to take distance courses at other participating institutions. The initiative also forms a partnership of research. Engaging in $8 billion in research in 2010, CIC universities are providing powerful insight into important issues in medicine, technology, agriculture, and communities.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Students at participating schools are also allowed &quot;in-house&quot; viewing privileges at other participating schools' libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> They also employ collective purchasing, which has saved member institutions $19 million to date.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_Park">Research Park</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Research Park">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Located in the southwest part of campus, <a href="/wiki/Research_Park,_University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana-Champaign" title="Research Park, University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign">Research Park</a> opened its first building in 2001 and has now grown to encompass 13 total buildings. 90 total companies have established roots in research park, employing over 1,400 employees. Companies also employee about 400 total student interns at any given time throughout the year.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Competition">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>According to the statistics of the 2008 admitted freshmen, 77% of incoming students had <a href="/wiki/ACT_(examination)" title="ACT (examination)" class="mw-redirect">ACT</a> score of 27 or higher, 31% had an <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> combined Math &amp; Critical Reading score above 1,400 (excludes Writing), and 59% of the incoming students were top 10% of their high school class.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of the university's colleges admit students at an even more competitive level. For incoming freshmen in 2008, the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Engineering" title="UIUC College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a> reported an ACT score <a href="/wiki/Interquartile_range" title="Interquartile range">interquartile range</a> of 30?33, the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Business" title="UIUC College of Business">College of Business</a> reported an ACT score IQR of 28?32, and the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Media" title="UIUC College of Media">College of Media</a>, in 2008, the first year it accepted freshmen, reported an ACT IQR of 27?32, higher than the overall campus median (though still lower than that of the College of Engineering). Of graduates, Illinois ended up as one of the top 12 (percentage) and top 6 (numerical) feeder state colleges to elite professional schools.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residences">Residences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Residences">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>University Residence Halls and University Private-Certified Housing are administered by the University's housing division.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> University housing for undergraduates is provided through twenty-four <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">residence halls</a> in both Urbana and Champaign. All incoming freshmen are required to live in certified student housing their first year on campus.</p> 
     <p>All undergraduates within the University housing system are required to purchase some level of meal plan, although they are free to eat elsewhere if they choose. Graduate housing is usually offered through two graduate residence halls, restricted to students who are sophomores or above, and through three university-owned apartment complexes. Students with disabilities are provided special housing options to accommodate their needs. The University of Illinois Urbana-Champaign is well known for being one of the first universities to provide accommodations for students with disabilities.</p> 
     <p>There are a number of private dormitories around campus, as well as a few houses that are outside of the Greek system and offer a more communal living experience. The private dorms tend to be more expensive to live in compared to other housing options. Private, certified residences maintain reciprocity agreements with the University, allowing students to move between the public and private housing systems if they are dissatisfied with their living conditions.</p> 
     <p>Some undergraduates choose to move into apartments or the Greek houses after their second year. The University Tenant Union offers advice on choosing apartments and the process of signing a lease.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Registered_student_organizations">Registered student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Registered student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University boasts over 1,000 active Registered Student Organizations (RSOs),<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> showcased at the start of each academic year during Illinois's &quot;Quad Day.&quot; Registration and support is provided by the Student Programs &amp; Activities Office, an administrative arm established in pursuit of the larger social, intellectual, and educative goals of the Illini Student Union. The Office's mission is to &quot;enhance ... classroom education,&quot; &quot;meet the needs and desires of the campus community,&quot; and &quot;prepare students to be contributing and humane citizens.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Fraternities_and_Sororities_at_University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana-Champaign" title="List of Fraternities and Sororities at University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign" class="mw-redirect">List of Fraternities and Sororities at University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The university has the largest Greek system in the world by membership.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UIUCstats_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UIUCstats-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> There are currently 59 fraternities and 36 sororities on the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Of the approximately 31,180 undergraduates,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> about 3,330 are members of sororities<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> and about 3,370 are members of fraternities. The Greek system at the University of Illinois has a system of self-government. While there are staff advisors and directors in charge of managing certain aspects of the Greek community, most of the day to day operations of the Greek community are governed by the Interfraternity Council and <a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_Panhellenic&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="University of Illinois Panhellenic (page does not exist)">Panhellenic Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of the fraternity and sorority houses on campus are on the National Register of Historic Places.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>U of I has an extensive history of past student governments. A mere two years after the university opened in 1868, John Milton Gregory and a group of students created a <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a> for a student government. Their governance expanded to the entire university in 1873, having a legislative, executive, and judicial branch. For a period of time, this government had the ability to discipline students. In 1883, however, due to a combination of events from Gregory's resignation to student-faculty infighting, the government formally dissolved itself via <a href="/wiki/Plebiscite" title="Plebiscite" class="mw-redirect">plebiscite</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>It wasn't until 1934, when the Student Senate, the next university-wide student government, was created. A year before, future U of I Dean of Students, Fred H. Turner and the university's Senate Committee on Student Affairs gave increased power to the Student Council, an organization primarily known for organizing dances. A year after, the Student Council created a constitution and became the Student Senate, under the oversight of the Committee on Student Affairs. The Student Senate would become the longest lasting student government in UIUC history, lasting for 35 years.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Student Senate changed its purpose and name in 1969, when it became the Undergraduate Student Association (UGSA). It no longer was a representational government, instead becoming an <a href="/wiki/Collective_bargaining_agency" title="Collective bargaining agency" class="mw-redirect">collective bargaining agency</a>. It often worked with the Graduate Student Association to work on various projects<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1967, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_A._Morrison" title="Bruce A. Morrison" class="mw-redirect">Bruce A. Morrison</a> and other U of I graduates founded the Graduate Student Association (GSA). GSA would last until 1978, when it merged with the UGSA to form the Champaign-Urbana Student Association (CUSA).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-illinois1948_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illinois1948-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>CUSA lasted for only 2 years when it was replaced by the Student Government Association (SGA) in 1980. SGA lasted for 15 years until it became the Illinois Student Government (ISG) in 1995. ISG lasted until 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-illinois1948_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illinois1948-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The current university student government, created in 2004, is the Illinois Student Senate, a combined undergraduate and graduate student senate with 54 voting members. The student senators are elected by college and represent the students in the Urbana-Champaign Senate (which comprises both faculty and students), as well as on a variety of faculty and administrative committees, and are led by an internally elected executive board of a President, External Vice President, Internal Vice President, and Treasurer. As of 2012, the executive board is supported by an executive staff consisting of a Chief of Staff, Clerk of the Senate, Parliamentarian, Director of Communications, Intern Coordinator, and the Historian of the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.library.illinois.edu/">campus library system</a> is one of the largest public academic collections in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-illinois2_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illinois2-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Among universities in North America, only the collections of Harvard are larger.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently, the University of Illinois' 20+ departmental libraries and divisions hold more than 24 <a href="/wiki/Million" title="Million">million</a> items, including more than 12 million print volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-illinois2_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illinois2-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2012, it had also the largest &quot;browsable&quot; university library in the United States, with 5 million volumes directly accessible in stacks in a single location.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> University of Illinois also has the largest public engineering library (<a href="/wiki/Grainger_Engineering_Library" title="Grainger Engineering Library">Grainger Engineering Library</a>) in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The online catalog is used by over one million people monthly<sup id="cite_ref-illinois2_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illinois2-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> and each day more than 50,000 articles are downloaded from electronic journals licensed by the University of Illinois Library.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to the main library building, which houses nearly 10 subject-oriented libraries, the Isaac Funk Family Library on the South Quad serves the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Agriculture,_Consumer,_and_Environmental_Sciences" title="UIUC College of Agriculture, Consumer, and Environmental Sciences">College of Agriculture, Consumer, and Environmental Sciences</a> and the Grainger Engineering Library Information Center serves the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_College_of_Engineering" title="UIUC College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a> on the <a href="/wiki/UIUC_Engineering_Campus" title="UIUC Engineering Campus">John Bardeen Quad</a>.</p> 
     <p>The University of Illinois Residence Hall Library System<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> is one of three in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The Residence Hall Libraries were created in 1948 to serve the educational, recreational, and cultural information needs of first and second year undergraduate students residing in the residence halls, and the living-learning communities within the residence halls. The collection also serves University Housing staff as well as the larger campus community, including undergraduate and graduate students, and university faculty and staff.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>All together there are more than 20 departmental or school libraries on campus.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Recently, the two main recreation facilities, <a href="/w/index.php?title=UIUC_Campus_Recreation_Center_-_East&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="UIUC Campus Recreation Center - East (page does not exist)">CRCE</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Activities_and_Recreation_Center" title="Activities and Recreation Center">Activities and Recreation Center</a> (ARC, formerly known as IMPE), were renovated.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The bus system that operates throughout the campus and community is operated by the <a href="/wiki/Champaign-Urbana_Mass_Transit_District" title="Champaign-Urbana Mass Transit District">Champaign-Urbana Mass Transit District</a>. The MTD receives a student-approved transportation fee from the university, which provides <a href="/wiki/Universal_transit_pass" title="Universal transit pass">unlimited access</a> for university students. In addition, the university pays for universal access for all its faculty and staff. As part of this arrangement, the MTD also runs a bus line between <a href="/wiki/The_University_of_Illinois_Willard_Airport" title="The University of Illinois Willard Airport" class="mw-redirect">Willard Airport</a> and Illinois Terminal, a multi-modal transportation facility which includes <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">Greyhound</a> ? making it the focal point of <a href="/wiki/Champaign-Urbana_Metropolitan_Area" title="Champaign-Urbana Metropolitan Area" class="mw-redirect">Champaign-Urbana's</a> public transportation systems.</p> 
     <p>The university maintains an extensive system of off-street <a href="/wiki/Bike_path" title="Bike path" class="mw-redirect">bike paths</a> and on-street bike lanes on campus. All students are expected to register their bicycles with the campus <a href="/wiki/Public_Safety" title="Public Safety" class="mw-redirect">public safety</a> department.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics_and_sports">Athletics and sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Athletics and sports">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Fighting_Illini" title="Illinois Fighting Illini">Illinois Fighting Illini</a>
     </div> 
     <p>U of I's Division of Intercollegiate Athletics fields teams for ten men's and eleven women's varsity sports. The university participates in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s Division I. The university's athletic teams are known as the Fighting Illini. The university operates a number of athletic facilities, including <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Stadium_(Champaign)" title="Memorial Stadium (Champaign)">Memorial Stadium</a> for <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>, the <a href="/wiki/State_Farm_Center" title="State Farm Center">State Farm Center</a> for men's and women's basketball, and the Atkins Tennis Center for men's and women's tennis. The men's NCAA basketball team had a dream run in the <a href="/wiki/2005_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="2005 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">2005 season</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Weber_(coach)" title="Bruce Weber (coach)" class="mw-redirect">Bruce Weber</a>'s Fighting Illini tying the record for most victories in a season. Their run ended 37?2 with a loss to the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball">North Carolina Tar Heels</a> in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">national championship game</a>.</p> 
     <p>Illinois is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>.</p> 
     <p>On October 15, 1910, the Illinois football team defeated the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> Maroons with a score of 3?0 in a game that Illinois claims was the first <a href="/wiki/Homecoming" title="Homecoming">homecoming</a> game, though several other schools claim to have held the first homecoming as well.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On November 10, 2007, the unranked Illinois football team defeated the No. 1 ranked <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State" title="Ohio State" class="mw-redirect">Ohio State</a> football team in <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Stadium" title="Ohio Stadium">Ohio Stadium</a>, the first time that the Illini beat a No. 1 ranked team on the road.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_Ice_Arena" title="University of Illinois Ice Arena">University of Illinois Ice Arena</a> is home to the university's club <a href="/wiki/College_ice_hockey" title="College ice hockey">college ice hockey</a> team competing at the <a href="/wiki/American_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="American Collegiate Hockey Association">ACHA Division I</a> level and is also available for recreational use through the Division of Campus Recreation. It was built in 1931 and designed by Chicago architecture firm Holabird and Root, the same firm that designed the University of Illinois Memorial Stadium and Chicago's Soldier Field. It is located on Armory Drive across from the Armory. The structure features 4 rows of bleacher seating in an elevated balcony that runs the length of the ice rink on either side. These bleachers provide seating for roughly 1,200 fans, with standing room and bench seating available underneath. Because of this set-up the team benches are actually directly underneath the stands.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Chief_Illiniwek" title="Chief Illiniwek">Chief Illiniwek</a>, or 'The Chief', was the university's official athletic symbol from 1926 until February 21, 2007. Use of the Chief garnered criticism for the university starting in the mid-1970s from Native Americans and others as a misappropriation and inaccurate portrayal of indigenous culture. The university officials announced the end of the Chief Illiniwek era on February 16, 2007.</p> 
     <p>Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic games are: <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Loyalty" title="Illinois Loyalty">Illinois Loyalty</a>, the school song, <a href="/wiki/Oskee_Wow_Wow" title="Oskee Wow Wow" class="mw-redirect">Oskee Wow Wow</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marching_Illini#Hail_to_the_Orange" title="Marching Illini">Hail to the Orange</a>, the alma mater.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_awards_and_recognition">Academic awards and recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Academic awards and recognition">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_honors">University honors</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: University honors">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>University Honors is an academic distinction awarded to high achieving students at UIUC. It is comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Latin_honors" title="Latin honors">Latin honors</a> of <a href="/wiki/Summa_cum_laude" title="Summa cum laude" class="mw-redirect">summa cum laude</a>. Graduating students awarded <i>University Honors</i> must have a cumulative grade point average of a 3.5/4.0 within the academic year of their graduation and rank within the top 3% of their graduating class.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="James_Scholars">James Scholars</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: James Scholars">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>&quot;James Scholars&quot; are undergraduate students invited to pursue a specialized course of study for no less than two years of their undergraduate course work. James Scholars can be admitted as such, or join in later. For the Engineering College, one is admitted immediately if they either score a 33 or higher on the ACT (or the SAT equivalent), or are in the top 1% of their high school graduating class.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Students can apply to be James Scholars if they hold a particular GPA at UIUC, which is dependent on the college and/or major. For the Engineering College, you can join or maintain James Scholar status if you hold a 3.30 /4.00 GPA, unless you are an ECE (Electrical and Computer Engineering) major, in which case you must hold a 3.50/4.00 GPA.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> James Scholars who graduate with &quot;University Honors&quot; are also awarded the Latin honors of <a href="/wiki/In_cursu_honorum" title="In cursu honorum">In cursu honorum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chancellor.27s_Scholars">Chancellor's Scholars</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Chancellor's Scholars">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>&quot;Chancellor's Scholars&quot; are undergraduate students in the Campus Honors Program, a campus-wide scholarship program which focuses on both academic excellence and leadership. Unlike James Scholars, only about 125 members may be admitted in a given year with a cap around 500 students at any given time. Chancellor's Scholars must have a grade point average of 3.3/4.0, successfully complete a total of five CHP sponsored courses, and participate in a specified number of CHP co-curricular events and activities.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_100_Honorary">Senior 100 Honorary</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Senior 100 Honorary">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>&quot;Senior 100 Honorary&quot; is an award from the Student Alumni Ambassadors and the University of Illinois Alumni Association that recognizes outstanding seniors. Recipients of this award are honored for their outstanding achievements in leadership, academics and campus involvement throughout their undergraduate education.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty_and_alumni">Notable faculty and alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notable faculty and alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign_people" title="List of University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign people">List of University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UIUC_Alma_Mater_Commencement_Week_2012_.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/UIUC_Alma_Mater_Commencement_Week_2012_.jpg/220px-UIUC_Alma_Mater_Commencement_Week_2012_.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/UIUC_Alma_Mater_Commencement_Week_2012_.jpg/330px-UIUC_Alma_Mater_Commencement_Week_2012_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/UIUC_Alma_Mater_Commencement_Week_2012_.jpg/440px-UIUC_Alma_Mater_Commencement_Week_2012_.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UIUC_Alma_Mater_Commencement_Week_2012_.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alma_Mater_(UIUC)_Commencement_Week&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alma Mater (UIUC) Commencement Week (page does not exist)">Alma Mater</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As of 2007, 21 alumni and faculty members are <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel</a> laureates and 20 have won a <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UIUCstats_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UIUCstats-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> In particular, <a href="/wiki/John_Bardeen" title="John Bardeen">John Bardeen</a> is the only person to have won two Nobel prizes in physics, having done so in 1956 and 1972 while on faculty at the University of Illinois. In 2003, two faculty members won Nobel prizes in different disciplines: <a href="/wiki/Paul_C._Lauterbur" title="Paul C. Lauterbur" class="mw-redirect">Paul C. Lauterbur</a> for physiology or medicine, and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Leggett" title="Anthony Leggett" class="mw-redirect">Anthony Leggett</a> for physics. Most recently, in 2007, Don Wuebbles, Atul Jain, John Walsh and Michael Schlesinger, professors in the Department of Atmospheric Science, were awarded a share of the Nobel Peace Prize for their contributions and collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/IPCC" title="IPCC" class="mw-redirect">IPCC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Fazlur_Rahman_Khan" title="Fazlur Rahman Khan" class="mw-redirect">Fazlur Rahman Khan</a>, considered to be the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Einstein</a> of <a href="/wiki/Structural_engineering" title="Structural engineering">structural engineering</a>&quot; and the &quot;Greatest Structural Engineer of the 20th century&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Alumni have created companies and products such as <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Communications" title="Netscape Communications" class="mw-redirect">Netscape Communications</a>, <a href="/wiki/AMD" title="AMD" class="mw-redirect">AMD</a>, <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siebel_Systems" title="Siebel Systems">Siebel Systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mortal_Kombat_(series)" title="Mortal Kombat (series)" class="mw-redirect">Mortal Kombat</a>, <a href="/wiki/CDW" title="CDW">CDW</a>, YouTube, <a href="/wiki/THX" title="THX">THX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Software" title="Lotus Software">Lotus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mosaic_(web_browser)" title="Mosaic (web browser)">Mosaic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safari_(web_browser)" title="Safari (web browser)">Safari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a>, <a href="/wiki/W._W._Grainger" title="W. W. Grainger">W. W. Grainger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>.</p> 
     <p>Alumni and faculty have invented the <a href="/wiki/LED" title="LED" class="mw-redirect">LED</a>, <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">integrated circuit</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Quantum_well_laser" title="Quantum well laser">quantum well laser</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">transistor</a>, <a href="/wiki/MRI" title="MRI" class="mw-redirect">MRI</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Plasma_screen" title="Plasma screen" class="mw-redirect">plasma screen</a>, and are responsible for the structural design of such buildings as the <a href="/wiki/Willis_Tower" title="Willis Tower">Willis Tower</a>, the <a href="/wiki/John_Hancock_Center" title="John Hancock Center">John Hancock Center</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Alumni have founded many organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Susan_G._Komen_for_the_Cure" title="Susan G. Komen for the Cure">Susan G. Komen for the Cure</a> and <a href="/wiki/Project_Gutenberg" title="Project Gutenberg">Project Gutenberg</a>, and have served in a wide variety of government and public interest roles. <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">Rafael Correa</a>, President of <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">The Republic of Ecuador</a> since January 2006 secured his M.S. and PhD degrees from the University's Economics Department in 1999 and 2001 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Clifford_Ricker" title="Nathan Clifford Ricker">Nathan C. Ricker</a> attended U of I and in 1873 was the first person to graduate in the United States with a degree in Architecture. Mary L. Page, the first woman to obtain a degree in architecture, also graduated from U of I.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Philanthropy is playing an increasingly significant role in supporting the Land Grant mission of the University of Illinois. The portion of the university's annual $1.5 billion budget which is state funds has diminished drastically over the past two decades. Currently the university receives only 16.4% of its budget from state tax dollars compared to 20 years ago when it received 44.5% of its budget from state tax dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-illinois1_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illinois1-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Gifts, grants, and contracts to the university comprise 19% of the annual budget.</p> 
     <p>Philanthropic giving to the university comes in the form of annual giving, major gifts, and estate planning. Annual giving is generally unrestricted by the donor and can be spent by the campus to meet immediate needs to maintain basic operations. Major gifts are typically put into an endowment at the donor's wishes, where the principal of the gift is invested while the interest is distributed to the campus department in which the donor designated their gift to be used. This practice of investing the principal in an endowment and only spending the interest, is done to secure the gift in perpetuity. In some cases, major gifts are used immediately for building campaigns such as the <a href="/wiki/Krannert_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Krannert Center for the Performing Arts">Krannert Center for the Performing Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Beckman_Institute" title="The Beckman Institute" class="mw-redirect">The Beckman Institute</a>, or <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Thomas_M._Siebel_Center_for_Computer_Science&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Thomas M. Siebel Center for Computer Science (page does not exist)">The Thomas M. Siebel Center for Computer Science</a>. Estate planning is another type of giving whereby a donor makes provisions in their will or estate documents which identifies the University of Illinois as a beneficiary.</p> 
     <p>Alumni play the largest role in philanthropic giving to the university. The most notable donors are <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Siebel" title="Thomas Siebel">Thomas M. Siebel</a> and his wife Stacey who recently gave a $100 million estate gift to the university after they had given $36 million to build the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thomas_M._Siebel_Center_for_Computer_Science&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thomas M. Siebel Center for Computer Science (page does not exist)">Thomas M. Siebel Center for Computer Science</a>, $10 million to endow the Siebel Scholars program, $2 million to endow the Thomas M. Siebel Chair in Computer Science and $2 million to endow the Thomas M. Siebel Chair in the History of Science. Other notable donors include <a href="/wiki/Sohaib_Abbasi" title="Sohaib Abbasi">Sohaib Abbasi</a> and his wife, Sara, who established the Sohaib and Sara Abbasi Professorship to enable the CS department to maintain its stature as one of the nation's premiere departments and give students the opportunity to learn from a world-renowned computer scientist and educator. They have also endowed the Sohaib and Sara Abbasi Fellowship to allow up to 5 graduate students each year, the opportunity to study computer science at one of the nation's top ranked computer science departments.</p> 
     <p>Stanley O. and Judith L. Ikenberry were the 14th President and First Lady of the Urbana-Champaign campus of the University of Illinois from 1979?1995. The Ikenberrys established the Stanley O. and Judith L. Ikenberry Endowment for Krannert Center for the Performing Arts. This gift supports the presentation of guest artists at the Center as part of the Marquee Endowment.</p>
