       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_THES_W_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_THES_W-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>31</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>In its 2012 listings, <i><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings#United_States" title="College and university rankings">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked the undergraduate program 45th among nationally accredited universities and 13th among nationally accredited public universities.<sup id="cite_ref-colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The graduate program had 60 disciplines ranked within the top 30 nationwide, including 23 within the top five. U.S. News &amp; World Report ranked the undergraduate and graduate Accounting programs 2nd and 4th respectively in the United States in their 2011 rankings; both programs had been ranked 1st at the same time in previous years. The College of Business as a whole was ranked 12th nationally. The College of Engineering was ranked 5th at the graduate level, with 14 disciplines ranked within the top ten. Chemistry and Physics were also ranked within the top ten at the graduate level. The College of Education had six programs ranked within the top ten. The Graduate School of Library and Information Science was ranked 1st, with five programs ranked within the top ten. Many arts programs were ranked within the first quartile, such as Architecture and Fine Arts. The Computer Science, Material Science, Agricultural Engineering, Civil Engineering, Electrical and Computer Engineering, Mechanical Engineering, Accounting, Finance, and Psychology are the university's most visibly distinguished departments. The School of Labor and Employment Relations is ranked consistently within the top two in the nation, behind only <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>.</p> 
     <p>The University of Illinois is considered a &quot;<a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a>&quot; and is measured comprehensively as one of the top 20 major research universities in the United States by a Graham-Diamond Report.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>International rankings by The Institute of Higher Education at <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a> suggest that Illinois is the 19th best university in North America, and 25th best university in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-shanghai_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghai-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The Academic Ranking of World Universities by Broad Subject Fields from the same research center in 2008 positions Illinois in 3rd for Engineering/Technology and Computer Sciences in the world. It is ranked 19th for Life and Agriculture Sciences, 20th for Natural Sciences and Mathematics, and 51st for Social Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-ARWU-FIELD-2007_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARWU-FIELD-2007-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2012, Illinois was ranked 56th in the world by <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> increasing its position from the 2009 <a href="/wiki/THE-QS_World_University_Rankings" title="THE-QS World University Rankings" class="mw-redirect">THE-QS World University Rankings</a> (in 2010, <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> and <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> parted ways to produce separate rankings). However, Illinois had been ranked within the top 40 in the past. The THE-QS rankings have been criticized due to their volatility: it stressed international popularity and ranks fluctuated tens of places from one year to the next.<sup id="cite_ref-AJUEHolmes_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJUEHolmes-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The WSJ ranking of business schools also has this inherited anomaly, attributable to its survey method.</p> 
     <p>The Institute for Labor and Industrial Relations has been recognized consistently as one of the top three programs for Human Resources and Labor Relations studies in the United States<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (July 2008)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p> 
     <p>In the 2008 release of <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a> by Cybermetrics Lab, which is a research unit of the National Research Council of Spain, the University was ranked 9th.<sup id="cite_ref-Webometrics2007_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Webometrics2007-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, <a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings#G-factor" title="College and university rankings">G-Factor</a>, another academic list trying to measure social network efficacy of universities, has ranked Illinois within the top eight.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> A human competitiveness index and analysis by the Human Resources &amp; Labor Review, and published in Chasecareer Network, ranked the university 25th internationally in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2007, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a> ranks Illinois as the 11th best university in the nation, and 9th among public universities. The methodology of the ranking includes &quot;how well it performs as an engine of social mobility,&quot; &quot;how well it does in fostering scientific and humanistic research,&quot; and &quot;how well it promotes an ethic of service to country.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonMonthly_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonMonthly-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Newsweek_International" title="Newsweek International" class="mw-redirect">Newsweek International</a> listed Illinois as one of Top 100 Global Universities,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> which &quot;takes into account openness and diversity, as well as distinction in research.&quot; <a href="/wiki/Kiplinger%27s_Personal_Finance" title="Kiplinger's Personal Finance">Kiplinger's Personal Finance</a> also listed Illinois in its 100 Best Values in Public Colleges,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> which &quot;measures academic quality, cost and financial aid.&quot;</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" title="Princeton Review" class="mw-redirect">Princeton Review</a> has elected Illinois one of the 366 best colleges out of nearly 5,000 degree-granting institutions of higher education in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Nonetheless, the university has come under criticism for its use of graduate teaching assistants in teaching undergraduate courses, including upper-level undergraduate courses. For two consecutive years, the Urbana?Champaign campus topped this review's<sup id="cite_ref-PrincetonReview_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrincetonReview-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> category of &quot;teaching assistants teach too many upper level courses.&quot; However, the Princeton Review's ranking has been scrutinized for its lack of accountability as the Review's ranking categorical data rely mainly upon student random sampling.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.932009_admissions_scandal">2005?2009 admissions scandal</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 2005?2009 admissions scandal">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_clout_scandal" title="University of Illinois clout scandal">University of Illinois clout scandal</a>
     </div> 
     <p>A series of investigative reports by the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> noted that between 2005 and 2009 university trustees, president, chancellor, and other administrators pressured admissions officials into admitting under-qualified but politically well-connected applicants into the university.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Although University officials initially denied,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> then downplayed the existence of a &quot;clout list&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> the university later announced it would form a panel of internal and external representatives to review the past admissions process and determine possible changes.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Chicago Tribune</i> took the University to court for summary judgment, which was <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://epic.org/amicus/tribune/20110311_170232_ferpa_case.pdf">granted</a> in March 2011. The University appealed, and a number of organizations, including the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://epic.org">Electronic Privacy Information Center</a>, filed &quot;friend of the court&quot; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://epic.org/amicus/tribune/EPIC_brief_Chi_Trib_final.pdf">briefs</a> on behalf of both parties.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Howell_firing">Howell firing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Howell firing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In July 2010, The News-Gazette reported<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> that Dr. Kenneth Howell, an adjunct professor teaching Introduction to Catholic Thought, was fired for teaching the Roman Catholic positions on homosexuality. The <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Defense_Fund" title="Alliance Defense Fund" class="mw-redirect">Alliance Defense Fund</a> has taken up Dr. Howell's case, stating that his dismissal is a violation of <a href="/wiki/Academic_freedom" title="Academic freedom">academic freedom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First Amendment</a>. The University's position, as stated by Ann Mester, associate dean of the College of Arts and Sciences, is that Dr. Howell's comments &quot;violate university standards of inclusivity, which would then entitle us to have him discontinue his teaching arrangement with us.&quot;</p> 
     <p>Dr. Howell was reinstated by the University of Illinois as an adjunct instructor for the fall 2010 term to teach &quot;Introduction to Catholicism&quot;, resolving the situation for the time being.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> The university announced on July 28 that it would follow the recommendation of the Academic Senate's General University Policy Committee to begin paying the salary of instructors teaching Catholic studies courses. St. John's Catholic Newman Center previously paid instructor salaries. The matter is currently under review by the Academic Senate Committee on Academic Freedom and Tenure.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
